Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                                                                     ii
Executive Summary
This report presents the results of the traffic impacts of four proposed improvement projects in the
Midtown area of Milpitas, California. The improvement projects include the following:

1) Convert the eastbound Carlo Street On-Ramp at Calaveras Boulevard to an eastbound off-ramp. The
    existing on-ramp to Calaveras Boulevard is substandard in many respects: (1) the radii of the ramp is
    insufficient for vehicles on the ramp to match speeds with traffic on Calaveras Boulevard, (2) The
    lane drop taper at Calaveras Boulevard is far less than current design standards, (3) The length of
    merge (i.e. the distance before two full lanes become one lane) is insufficient for on-ramp traffic to
    safely locate a gap in traffic on eastbound Calaveras Boulevard. Eliminating this sub-standard merge
    would improve overall safety on eastbound Calaveras Boulevard between Milpitas Boulevard and
    Abel Street.

2) Reduce Main Street between Abel Street and Great Mall Parkway from five lanes (two lanes in each
   direction) to three lanes (one in each direction with a two way center left turn lane). The lane
   reduction will improve safety by reducing Main Street from four lanes to two lanes, which would
   allow for wider northbound and southbound bike lanes and a wider parking strip on the west side of
   Main Street. The improvement will not result in a lane reduction at the intersection of Great Mall
   Parkway/Main Street.

3) Eliminate future construction of a second left turn lane from eastbound Calaveras Boulevard to
   northbound Abel Street. This was a mitigation in the Midtown Milpitas Specific Plan EIR dated
   October 2001, but further study revealed that biology impacts, water quality impacts to Wrigley
   Creek, and land use/acquisition impacts would occur as a result of the improvement.

4) Modify signal phasing at the intersection of Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard to allow
   simultaneous southbound right-turn and eastbound left-turn movements. This improvement would
   improve overall traffic flow on Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard.

The potential impacts of the project were evaluated in accordance with the standards set forth by the City
of Milpitas and the Congestion Management Program (CMP) of Santa Clara County. The study included
an analysis of AM and PM peak hour traffic conditions for 15 signalized intersections and 3 unsignalized
intersections.

Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                   iii
Re-Assignment of Traffic
For the near-term analysis, the impact of converting the eastbound on-ramp at Calaveras Boulevard to an
eastbound off-ramp was evaluated in two phases. The first phase (hereafter referred to as Phase 1)
includes the closure of the on-ramp from Main Street to eastbound Calaveras Boulevard. During this
phase, access to eastbound Calaveras Boulevard from Main Street will be closed, but the off-ramp from
eastbound Calaveras Boulevard would not yet be opened. The second phase (hereafter referred to as
Phase 2) represents the full implementation of the improvement projects, including both the closure of the
on-ramp and the opening of the new off-ramp. Both Phases 1 and 2 of this analysis include all of the
other proposed improvement projects previously described.

The improvement project to rebuild the Carlo Street Ramp from an on-ramp to eastbound Calaveras
Boulevard to an off-ramp would change travel routes for drivers entering and exiting Midtown. The
changes are outlined below.

Phase 1 Diversion. With the on-ramp to Calaveras Boulevard eliminated, drivers exiting the Midtown
area would have two options for reaching eastern destinations. First, for traffic originating south of
Calaveras Boulevard on Main Street, drivers would likely divert to northbound Abel Street (via Serra
Way, Corning Avenue, or some other parallel route farther south) and make a right turn at the intersection
of Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard. Based on the existing traffic counts and the Midtown traffic
projections, the vast majority of traffic exiting Midtown would choose this route. Second, for traffic
originating north of Calaveras Boulevard on Main Street, drivers would likely divert to southbound Abel
Street (via Weller Lane) and turn left at the intersection of Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard. Overall,
for drivers exiting Midtown, the on-ramp closure would result in significantly more trips at the Abel
Street/Calaveras Boulevard intersection for the northbound right turn movement and southbound left turn
movement.

Phase 2 Diversion. The diversion for Phase 2 would include all of the diversion of Phase 1, plus it would
provide another primary route for drivers to enter Midtown. With the opening of the off-ramp from
Calaveras Boulevard to Main Street, drivers would have three primary routes to enter the Midtown area
from west Milpitas. First, eastbound drivers could choose to take Calaveras Boulevard just past Abel
Street to the new Carlo Street Off-Ramp. The off-ramp provides direct access to Midtown Milpitas.
Second, vehicles heading eastbound on Calaveras Boulevard could turn right on Serra Way, also
providing direct access to Midtown Milpitas. Due to the heavy traffic volumes on Calaveras Boulevard
during the PM peak, it is anticipated that many drivers will continue to utilize Serra Way to access
Midtown. Third, eastbound drivers on Calaveras Boulevard could choose to turn left at Abel Street to
access Weller Lane or Marylinn Drive to enter Midtown. However, with the proposed ramp conversion,
drivers would be less likely to make a left at Abel Street because the new ramp would provide a more
direct route for some destinations within Midtown. Overall, for drivers entering Midtown, the ramp
conversion would result in fewer trips eastbound on Serra Way and fewer trips for the eastbound left turn
movement at the Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard intersection. The ramp conversion would result in more
eastbound through trips at the intersection of Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard.

The peak hour trips generated by Phases 1 and 2 of the proposed ramp conversion were assigned to the
roadway system in accordance with the trip redistribution patterns discussed above. None of the other
project improvements would result in significant traffic diversion.




Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                   iv
Near Term Intersection Impacts and Mitigation
Project impacts were determined based on the appropriate significance criteria. The results of the
intersection level of service analysis show one of the signalized study intersections would be impacted by
the project (see Table ES-1).

     Significant Impact: The intersection of Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard would operate at LOS E
     under Near Term No Project conditions during the PM peak hour. Under Phase 1 and 2 project
     conditions it would degrade to LOS F. According to the CMP guidelines, this would constitute a
     significant impact.

Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                                                                   v
    Mitigation: The 2030 Valley Transportation Plan (VTP) includes a range of highway and transit
    improvement projects to ease existing and future traffic congestion along major travel corridors in
    Santa Clara County. The widening of Calaveras Boulevard, between Milpitas Boulevard and Abel
    Street, is the highest priority project under the Street and Local Roads category and at least 80% of
    the necessary project funding may be secured from federal sources as part of the VTP. To mitigate the
    significant impact, as part of the widening of Calaveras widening project, the following would be
    required:

    ·   Add one additional westbound left turn lane on Calaveras Boulevard (for a total of 2 left turn
        lanes), and
    ·   Restripe the northbound approach on Abel Street from a two through lanes and one right turn lane
        to one through lane, one shared right/through lane, and one right turn lane. This may require
        modifications to the crosswalks at the intersection.

    The implementation of this mitigation would return the LOS to E during the PM peak hour.
    However, the implementation of these improvements may have secondary affects that result in
    additional undesirable impacts. The addition of a second right turn lane northbound on Abel Street
    could result in safety issues for pedestrians in the adjacent crosswalk. While removal of the crosswalk
    would eliminate the potential safety issue, crosswalk removal would decrease pedestrian mobility in
    the Midtown area, which is contrary to the goals of the Midtown Specific Plan. In addition, the
    additional westbound left turn lane on Calaveras Boulevard results in alignment issues with the
    Calaveras Blvd PSR and additional right-of-way on Calaveras Boulevard. Furthermore, this
    improvement is not likely feasible without the widening of Calaveras Boulevard bridge between Abel
    Street and Milpitas Boulevard, which may not occur for many years. Considering all these issues, the
    City of Milpitas has decided that the Phase 1 and 2 impacts at Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard
    should be considered significant and unavoidable. Because Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard is
    designated as a CMP intersection, and the intersection is subject to regional monitoring, the City of
    Milpitas has opted to prepare a deficiency plan to offset the significant and unavoidable impacts at
    this location.


Year 2030 Traffic Analysis
The analysis of 2030 conditions was conducted only for the full build out of the four proposed
improvement projects (Phase 2 only). Phase 1 (onramp closure only) represents an interim condition
likely to occur during construction of the new off-ramp. It would be completed well in advance of 2030.

Project conditions were evaluated relative to No Project 2030 in order to determine potential impacts. As
expected, many of the roadway segments would operate a LOS E or F by the year 2030. Even though the
2030 roadway network assumes several major roadway capacity improvements, the anticipated growth in
jobs and housing would cause the traffic to increase substantially and cause increased congestion on the
transportation system.

The proposed improvement projects would have a beneficial significant impact on the following roadway
segments in both the AM and PM Peak Hour:

    ·   Main Street (southbound), between Calaveras Boulevard Ramp and Carlo Street Ramp (AM Peak)
    ·   Main Street (northbound), between Carlo Street Ramp and Curtis Avenue (PM Peak)
    ·   Main Street (southbound), between Calaveras Boulevard Ramp and Carlo Street Ramp (PM Peak)


Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                    vi
The proposed improvement projects would have an adverse significant impact the following roadway
segments in both the AM and PM peak hours:

    ·   Abel Street (southbound), between Milpitas Boulevard and Calaveras Boulevard (AM Peak)
    ·   Abel Street (northbound), between Calaveras Boulevard and Great Mall Parkway (PM Peak)
    ·   Main Street (northbound), between Weller Lane and Calaveras Boulevard Ramp (PM Peak)
    ·   Main Street (northbound), between Calaveras Boulevard Ramp and Carlo Street Ramp (PM Peak)

    Significant Impact: Abel Street southbound between Milpitas Boulevard and Calaveras Boulevard
    would operate at LOS F under No Project 2030 conditions during the AM peak hour. The Carlo Street
    ramp conversion would add traffic in the amount of 2% of capacity to this segment. According to the
    Milpitas significance criteria, this would constitute a significant impact. The significant impacts on
    Abel Street between Milpitas Boulevard and Calaveras Boulevard occur immediately around the
    intersection of Calaveras Boulevard at Abel Street. Thus, the improvements to this intersection would
    effectively mitigate the impacts of the Carlo Street ramp diversion. However, as previously described,
    for various reasons, the City has considered these improvements infeasible and considers the impacts
    on this segment to be significant and unavoidable.

    Significant Impact: Abel Street northbound between Calaveras Boulevard and Great Mall Parkway
    would operate at LOS E under No Project 2030 conditions during the PM peak hour. The Carlo Street
    ramp conversion would add traffic in the amount of 13% of capacity to this segment. According to
    the Milpitas significance criteria, this would constitute a significant impact. The significant impacts
    on Abel Street between Great Mall Parkway and Calaveras Boulevard occur immediately around the
    intersection of Calaveras Boulevard at Abel Street. Thus, the improvements to this intersection would
    effectively mitigate the impacts of the Carlo Street ramp diversion. However, as previously described,
    for various reasons, the City has considered these improvements infeasible and considers the impacts
    on this segment to be significant and unavoidable.

    Significant Impact: Main Street northbound between Weller Lane and Calaveras Boulevard Ramp
    would operate at LOS F under No Project 2030 conditions during the PM peak hour. The Carlo Street
    ramp conversion would add traffic in the amount of 2.8% of capacity to this segment. According to
    the Milpitas significance criteria, this would constitute a significant impact. Mitigation of significant
    project impacts on these segments of Main Street would require roadway widening to construct
    additional through lanes, thereby increasing roadway capacity. However, widening is not consistent
    with the City's North Main Street Streetscape Project, which is currently under construction and is
    intended to create a more walkable environment. Therefore, the significant impacts on this segment
    should be considered significant and unavoidable.

    Significant Impact: Main Street northbound between Calaveras Boulevard Ramp and Carlo Street
    Ramp would operate at LOS F under No Project 2030 conditions during the PM peak hour. The Carlo
    Street ramp conversion would add traffic in the amount of 2.1% of capacity to this segment.
    According to the Milpitas significance criteria, this would constitute a significant impact. Mitigation
    of significant project impacts on these segments of Main Street would require roadway widening to
    construct additional through lanes, thereby increasing roadway capacity. However, widening is not
    consistent with the City's North Main Street Streetscape Project, which is currently under construction
    and is intended to create a more walkable environment. Therefore, the significant impacts on this
    segment should be considered significant and unavoidable.

1.
Introduction
This report presents the results of the traffic impacts of four proposed improvement projects in the
Midtown area of Milpitas, California. The improvement projects include the following:

1) Convert the eastbound Carlo Street On-Ramp at Calaveras Boulevard to an eastbound off-ramp. The
   existing on-ramp to Calaveras Boulevard is substandard in many respects: (1) the radii of the ramp is
   insufficient for vehicles on the ramp to match speeds with traffic on Calaveras Boulevard, (2) The
   lane drop taper at Calaveras Boulevard is far less than current design standards. (3) The length of
   merge (i.e. the distance before two full lanes become one lane) is insufficient for on-ramp traffic to
   safely locate a gap in traffic on eastbound Calaveras Boulevard. Eliminating this sub-standard merge
   would improve overall safety on eastbound Calaveras Boulevard between Milpitas Boulevard and
   Abel Street.

2) Reduce Main Street between Abel Street and Great Mall Parkway from five lanes (two lanes in each
   direction) to three lanes (one in each direction with a two way center left turn lane). The lane
   reduction will improve safety by reducing Main Street from four lanes to two lanes, which would
   allow for wider northbound and southbound bike lanes and a wider parking strip on the west side of
   Main Street. The improvement will not result in a lane reduction at the intersection of Great Mall
   Parkway/Main Street.

3) Eliminate future construction of a second left turn lane from eastbound Calaveras Boulevard to
   northbound Abel Street. This was a mitigation in the Midtown Milpitas Specific Plan EIR dated
   October 2001, but further study revealed that biology impacts, water quality impacts to Wrigley
   Creek, and land use/acquisition impacts would occur as a result of the improvement.

4) Modify signal phasing at the intersection of Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard to allow
   simultaneous southbound right-turn and eastbound left-turn movements. This improvement would
   improve overall traffic flow on Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard.

The projects and the surrounding study area are shown on Figure 1. The Carlo Street ramp conversion is
shown graphically on Figure 2.

Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                      1
Scope of Study
This study was conducted for the purpose of identifying the potential traffic impacts of the four
previously described improvement projects relative to the existing Midtown Milpitas Specific Plan. This
analysis does not include an update of the impacts and mitigations required as a result of the land uses
contained in the Midtown Milpitas Specific Plan. The impacts of the project were evaluated following the
standards and methodologies set forth by the City of Milpitas and the Santa Clara Valley Transportation
Authority (VTA). The VTA administers the county Congestion Management Program (CMP). The traffic
analysis is based on peak hour levels of service for the study intersections. The traffic analysis also
includes an evaluation of peak hour signal warrants for the unsignalized intersections of Main
Street/Calaveras Boulevard Off-Ramp and Main Street/Carlo Street. The Main Street/Weller Lane
unsignalized intersection is reverting back to a signalized intersection prior to project completion.
Therefore, an evaluation of peak hour signal warrants is unnecessary for the intersection. The study
intersections are identified below.

                 I-880 SB Ramps and Calaveras Boulevard
                 I-880 NB Ramps and Calaveras Boulevard
                 Abbott Street and Calaveras Boulevard
                 Serra Way and Calaveras Boulevard
                 Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard*
                 Milpitas Boulevard and Calaveras Boulevard*
                 Town Center Drive and Calaveras Boulevard
                 Hillview Drive and Calaveras Boulevard
                 Abel Street and Marylinn Drive
                 Abel Street and Weller Lane
                 Abel Street and Serra Avenue
                 Abel Street and Corning Avenue
                 Abel Street and Main Street
                 Main Street and Weller Lane (unsignalized)
                 Main Street and Calaveras Boulevard Off-Ramp (unsignalized)
                 Main Street and Carlo Street (unsignalized)
                 Main Street and Serra Way
                 Main Street and Great Mall Parkway

CMP intersections are denoted with an asterisk (*).

Traffic conditions at the study intersections were analyzed for the weekday AM and PM peak hours of
traffic. The AM peak hour of traffic is generally between 7:00 and 9:00 AM, and the PM peak hour is
typically between 4:00 and 6:00 PM. It is during these periods that the most congested traffic conditions
occur on an average day. Traffic conditions were evaluated for the following scenarios:

   Scenario 1:     Existing Conditions. Existing conditions were represented by existing peak hour traffic
                   volumes on the existing roadway network. Existing traffic volumes were obtained from
                   the City of Milpitas.




Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                      2
    Scenario 2: Near Term No Project Conditions. Near Term No Project conditions were represented
                by future traffic volumes on the near-term future roadway network. Near Term No
                Project traffic volumes were estimated by adding to existing peak hour volumes the
                traffic from the Midtown Milpitas Specific Plan and the traffic volumes from approved
                but not yet completed developments. The latter components are contained in the City of
                Milpitas Approved Trips Inventory (ATI) and the North San Jose project.
    Scenario 3:    Project Conditions. Project conditions were represented by future traffic volumes, with
                   the proposed projects, on the near-term future roadway network. Future traffic volumes
                   with the project (hereafter called project traffic volumes) were estimated by adding to
                   Near Term No Project traffic volumes the diversion generated by the proposed projects.
                   The proposed improvement projects were evaluated relative to Near Term No Project
                   conditions in order to determine potential project impacts.

    Scenario 4 : Year 2030 Conditions. Future conditions were represented by year 2030 traffic volumes
                 with and without the proposed improvement projects. Base traffic volumes were
                 obtained from the McCarthy Ranch R&D TIA, dated September 25, 2007. Per City of
                 Milpitas requirements, roadway segments were evaluated for year 2030 conditions.


Methodology
This section presents the methods used to determine the traffic conditions for each scenario described
above. It includes descriptions of the data requirements, the analysis methodologies, and the applicable
level of service standards.

Data Requirements

The data required for the analysis were obtained from field observations, previous traffic studies, the City
of Milpitas, and the CMP annual Monitoring Report. The following data were collected from these
sources:

·   existing traffic volumes
·   lane configurations
·   signal timing and phasing (for signalized intersections only)
·   approved trips inventory for Milpitas
·   North San Jose Phase One
·   planned roadway improvements
·   Milpitas 2030 base year forecasts

Analysis Methodologies

Traffic conditions at the study locations were evaluated using level of service (LOS). Level of Service is a
qualitative description of operating conditions ranging from LOS A, or free-flow conditions with little or
no delay, to LOS F, or jammed conditions with excessive delays.

The City of Milpitas and CMP level of service methodologies utilize TRAFFIX software using CMP
default settings. TRAFFIX is based on the 2000 Highway Capacity Manual (HCM) method for
intersections, and evaluates intersection operations on the basis of average delay for all vehicles at the

Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                       5
intersection. This average delay can then be correlated to a level of service as shown in Table 1 for
signalized intersections. The level of service correlation for unsignalized intersections is shown in Table
2. For two-way stop controlled intersections, the level of service reported is for the worst approach of the
intersection.
Table 1
Signalized Intersection Level of Service Definitions Based on Delay

                                                                                                     Average
                                                                                                  Control Delay
  Level of                                                                                         Per Vehicle
  Service                                        Description                                        (seconds)

     A        Operations with very low delay occurring with favorable progression                  10.0 or less
              and/or short cycle lengths.
     B        Operations with low delay occurring with good progression and/or                     10.1 to 20.0
              short cycle lengths.
     C        Operations with average delays resulting from fair progression                       20.1 to 35.0
              and/or longer cycle lengths. Individual cycle failures begin to
              appear.
     D        Operations with longer delays due to a combination of unfavorable                    35.1 to 55.0
              progression, long cycle lengths, or high V/C ratios. Many vehicles
              stop and individual cycle failures are noticeable.
     E        Operations with high delay values indicating poor progression, long                  55.1 to 80.0
              cycle lengths, and high V/C ratios. Individual cycle failures are
               frequent occurrences. This is considered to be the limit of
              acceptable delay.
      F       Operation with delays unacceptable to most drivers occurring due                 Greater than 80.0
              to oversaturation, poor progression, or very long cycle lengths.

Source: Transportation Research Board, Highway Capacity Manual 2000, Exhibit 16-2.



Table 2
Unsignalized Intersection Level of Service Definitions Based on Delay

          Level of                                                                    Average Delay
          Service                    Description of Operations                       Per Vehicle (Sec.)

             A                         Little or no traffic delay                      10.0 or less
             B                           Short traffic delays                          10.1 to 15.0

             C                         Average traffic delays                          15.1 to 25.0
             D                           Long traffic delays                           25.1 to 35.0
             E                         Very long traffic delays                        35.1 to 50.0
             F                         Extreme traffic delays                        Greater than 50.0

Source: Transportation Research Board, 2000 Highway Capacity Manual (Washington, D.C., 2000) p17-2.




Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                             6
In addition to the level of service evaluation, for unsignalized intersections an assessment is made of the
need for signalization of the intersection. This assessment is made on the basis of the Peak hour Volume
Signal Warrant described in the Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices (MUTCD), 2003. This
method makes no evaluation of intersection level of service, but simply provides an indication whether
peak hour traffic volumes are, or would be, sufficient to justify installation of a traffic signal.

Roadway Segments

For 2030 conditions, the traffic operations at the study segments were calculated based on the volume-to-
capacity ratio, which can be correlated to a level of service. Table 3 shows the roadway types, capacity
assumptions, and LOS thresholds that were used for this analysis.

Arterial              900          540        630         720        810         900        >900




Level of Service Standards

For CMP intersections, roadway segments, and freeway segments, the minimum acceptable level of
service is LOS E. At intersections and roadway segments in Milpitas that are not CMP intersections, the
minimum acceptable level of service is LOS D.


Report Organization
The remainder of this report is divided into five chapters. Chapter 2 describes Existing Conditions in
terms of the existing roadway network and traffic volumes. Chapter 3 presents roadway operations under
Near Term No Project conditions. Chapter 4 describes the improvement projects impact on the
transportation system. Chapter 5 discusses the traffic conditions under year 2030 conditions.




Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                        7
2.
Existing Conditions
This chapter describes the existing conditions for all the major roadway facilities in the vicinity of the
site, including the roadway network, levels of service, and field observations.


Existing Roadway Network
Regional access to the Midtown area is provided via I-880, I-680, and SR 237/Calaveras Boulevard.
These facilities are described below.

        I-680 is a north/south freeway traversing the eastern portion of Milpitas. This freeway connects
        the inland East Bay communities to the north with San Jose to the south. I-680 has six mixed flow
        lanes north of SR 237 and eight mixed flow lanes south of SR 237. A southbound HOV lane is
        currently in operation north of Calaveras Boulevard.

        I-880 is a north/south freeway providing regional access from East Bay cities to San Jose, where
        it becomes SR 17. Within the City of Milpitas, I-880 is a six-to-eight lane freeway. The initial
        construction phases of the SR 237/I-880 interchange have recently been completed. South of
        Montague Expressway, I-880 has recently been widened to six lanes.

        State Route 237/Calaveras Boulevard is an east/west arterial between I-880 and I-680 and
        generally provides six travel lanes (four on the Union Pacific overcrossing). West of I-880, this
        facility becomes a freeway with four mixed flow lanes and two High Occupancy Vehicle (HOV)
        lanes. Calaveras Boulevard accommodates a significant amount of regional through traffic during
        the peak commute hours. Milpitas staff estimate that approximately 50 percent of the peak hour
        traffic between I-680 and I-880 is generated outside of Milpitas. The predominate direction of
        travel is westbound in the morning and eastbound during the afternoon.

Local access to the Midtown area is provided by Abel Street and Main Street. These roadways are
described below.



Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                       8
        Abel Street is a four-lane north/south arterial beginning at Main Street and terminating at Milpitas
        Boulevard. This roadway provides a two-way center left-turn lane along some segments. This
        facility is signalized at major cross streets, where left-turn pockets are provided. On-street
        parking is generally prohibited, except adjacent to residential frontage.

        Main Street is a north/south collector connecting Montague Expressway to residential areas north
        of Calaveras Boulevard. This roadway consists of four travel lanes from Montague Expressway to
        just north of Curtis Avenue, where it transitions to a two lane facility with parking on both sides.
        Main Street currently operates within capacity, but experiences peak hour congestion at its
        intersection with Montague Expressway.


Existing Intersection Lane Configurations & Traffic Volumes
The existing lane configurations at the study intersections were determined by observations in the field.
The existing intersection lane configurations are shown on Figure 3. Existing peak hour traffic volumes
were obtained from the City of Milpitas. The existing peak hour intersection volumes are shown on
Figure 4. The traffic count data are included in Appendix A.


Existing Intersection Level of Service

The level of service results for the signalized and unsignalized intersections under existing conditions are
summarized in Table 4. The results show that, measured against the City of Milpitas level of service
standards, all of the study intersections currently operate at acceptable levels. The level of service
calculation sheets are included in Appendix D.



Existing Signal Warrants
The peak hour signal warrant (MUTCD, 2003) was checked for the unsignalized intersections of Main
Street/Calaveras Boulevard Off-Ramp and Main Street/Carlo Street On-Ramp to determine whether
signalization would be justified on the basis of existing peak hour volumes. The analysis showed that the
peak hour volume signal warrant is not satisfied under existing conditions at any of the intersections.
However, this is just one of eleven possible signal warrants. The signal warrants analysis sheets are
included in Appendix E.


Observed Existing Traffic Conditions
Traffic conditions in the field were observed in order to identify existing operational deficiencies and to
confirm the accuracy of calculated levels of service. The purpose of this effort was (1) to identify any
existing traffic problems that may not be directly related to level of service, and (2) to identify any
locations where the level of service analysis does not accurately reflect existing traffic conditions.

Overall, the level of service analysis appears to accurately reflect actual existing traffic conditions.
However, field observations revealed that some operational problems do occur.




Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                        9
Hillview Drive and Calaveras Boulevard ­ During the PM peak hours, the eastbound traffic queue was
unable to clear the intersection in one signal cycle. Traffic queues would stretch past the Calaveras
Boulevard/Town Center Drive intersection to the west.

I-880 (NB ramps) and Calaveras Boulevard ­ During the PM peak hours, the westbound right turn queue
to I-880 North spills out into Calaveras Boulevard. A queue of fifteen cars was observed on Calaveras
Boulevard. This was caused by heavy traffic northbound on I-880.

It should be noted that Calaveras Boulevard, an eastern extension of SR 237, provides a link between the
major interstate highways I-880 and I-680. As expected, heavy traffic volumes were observed on
Calaveras Boulevard during commute hours. Intersections along Calaveras Boulevard operated well
considering the high traffic volumes.

3.
Near Term No Project Conditions
This chapter describes Near Term No Project traffic conditions. It shows the resulting levels of service at
the study intersections based on the most recent available traffic counts and assuming a Near Term
buildout of the Midtown Milpitas Specific Plan. Near Term No Project traffic volumes were estimated by
adding to existing peak hour volumes the traffic from the Midtown Milpitas Specific Plan and the traffic
volumes from approved but not yet completed developments. This chapter describes both the procedure
used to determine Near Term No Project traffic volumes and the resulting traffic conditions.


Near Term No Project Transportation Network & Traffic Volumes
It is assumed in this analysis that the future near-term roadway network at the study intersections would
be the same as existing conditions, except this scenario also includes the improvements required as
mitigation in the Midtown Milpitas Specific Plan EIR dated October 2001 as well as programmed Capital
Improvement Projects (CIP). These improvements include:

·   An additional eastbound left-turn at the Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard intersection (Midtown
    Milpitas Specific Plan EIR mitigation) and
·   Median improvements on Main Street and Abel Street (CIP Projects) and
·   Signalization of Main Street and Weller Lane.

Near Term No Project peak hour traffic volumes were calculated by adding to existing volumes the
estimated traffic from approved but not yet constructed developments and traffic from the Midtown
Milpitas Specific Plan. The added traffic from approved but not yet constructed developments was
provided by Milpitas in the form of an Approved Trips Inventory (ATI). Trips from the North San Jose
Phase One buildout were also added to the ATI. Traffic from the buildout of Midtown was estimated from
the Midtown Milpitas Specific Plan EIR dated October 2001. In cases where Midtown Milpitas Specific
Plan development traffic was also included in the Milpitas ATI or has been built, the duplication of trips
was removed from the Near Term No Project traffic volume estimates. Near Term No Project traffic
volumes are shown on Figure 5. A full description of the ATI is included in Appendix B.



Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                   14
Near Term No Project Intersection Analysis
The results of the intersection level of service analysis under Near Term No Project conditions are
summarized in Table 5. The results show that the intersection of Milpitas Boulevard/Calaveras Boulevard
would operate at LOS F during the AM peak hour. The remaining study intersections would operate at an
acceptable LOS. The level of service calculation sheets are included in Appendix D.


Near Term No Project Signal Warrants
The peak hour signal warrant (MUTCD, 2003) was checked at the unsignalized intersections of Main
Street/Calaveras Boulevard Off-Ramp and Main Street/Carlo Street On-Ramp to determine whether
signalization would be justified on the basis of Near Term No Project peak hour volumes. The analysis
showed that the peak hour volume signal warrant is not satisfied under Near Term No Project conditions
at any the intersections. However, this is just one of eleven possible signal warrants checks. The signal
warrant analysis sheets are included in Appendix E.

4.
Project Impacts and Mitigation Measures
This chapter describes project traffic conditions, significant project impacts, and measures that are
recommended to mitigate impacts. Included are descriptions of the significance criteria that define an
intersection impact, estimates of project-generated traffic, identification of the impacts, and descriptions
of the mitigation measures. Project conditions are represented by Near Term No Project traffic conditions
plus the implementation of the four proposed improvement projects.

Transportation Network Under Project Conditions
The proposed improvement projects would make the following changes to the roadway network. Other
than these changes, it is assumed in this analysis that the near-term roadway network under project
conditions would be the same as described under Near Term No Project conditions.

1.   Convert the eastbound Carlo Street On-Ramp at Calaveras Boulevard to an eastbound off-ramp

2. Reduce Main Street between Abel Street and Great Mall Parkway from five lanes (two lanes in each
   direction) to three lanes (one in each direction with a two way center left turn lane). This
   improvement will not result in a lane reduction at the intersection of Great Mall Parkway/ Main
   Street. At the intersection of Abel Street/Main Street, the westbound right turn traffic island will be
   removed and the number of approach lanes on Main Street will be reduced from three to two.

3. Eliminate future construction of a second left turn lane from eastbound Calaveras Boulevard to
   northbound Abel Street.

4. Modify signal phasing at the intersection of Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard to allow
   simultaneous southbound right-turn and eastbound left-turn movements.

For the purposes of this analysis, the impact of converting the eastbound on-ramp at Calaveras Boulevard
to an eastbound off-ramp was evaluated in two phases. The first phase (hereafter referred to as Phase 1)
includes the closure of the on-ramp from Main Street to eastbound Calaveras Boulevard. During this
phase, access to eastbound Calaveras Boulevard from Main Street will be closed, but the off-ramp from
eastbound Calaveras Boulevard would not yet be opened. The second phase (hereafter referred to as

Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                    18
Phase 2) represents the full implementation of the improvement projects, including both the closure of the
on-ramp and the opening of the new off-ramp. Both Phases 1 and 2 of this analysis include all of the
other proposed improvement projects described above.


Re-Assignment of Traffic
The improvement project to rebuild the Carlo Street Ramp from an on-ramp to eastbound Calaveras
Boulevard to an off-ramp would change travel routes for drivers entering and exiting Midtown. The
changes are outlined below.

Phase 1 Diversion. With the on-ramp to Calaveras Boulevard eliminated, drivers exiting the Midtown
area would have two options for reaching eastern destinations. First, for traffic originating south of
Calaveras Boulevard on Main Street, drivers would likely divert to northbound Abel Street (via Serra
Way, Corning Avenue, or some other parallel route farther south) and make a right turn at the intersection
of Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard. Based on the existing traffic counts and the Midtown traffic
projections, the vast majority of traffic exiting Midtown would choose this route. Second, for traffic
originating north of Calaveras Boulevard on Main Street, drivers would likely divert to southbound Abel
Street (via Weller Lane) and turn left at the intersection of Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard. Overall,
for drivers exiting Midtown, the on-ramp closure would result in significantly more trips at the Abel
Street/Calaveras Boulevard intersection for the northbound right turn movement and southbound left turn
movement.

Phase 2 Diversion. The diversion for Phase 2 would include all of the diversion of Phase 1, plus it would
provide another primary route for drivers to enter Midtown. With the opening of the off-ramp from
Calaveras Boulevard to Main Street, drivers would have three primary routes to enter the Midtown area
from west Milpitas. First, eastbound drivers could choose to take Calaveras Boulevard just past Abel
Street to the new Carlo Street Off-Ramp. The off-ramp provides direct access to Midtown Milpitas.
Second, vehicles heading eastbound on Calaveras Boulevard could turn right on Serra Way, also
providing direct access to Midtown Milpitas. Due to the heavy traffic volumes on Calaveras Boulevard
during the PM peak, it is anticipated that many drivers will continue to utilize Serra Way to access
Midtown. Third, eastbound drivers on Calaveras Boulevard could choose to turn left at Abel Street to
access Weller Lane or Marylinn Drive to enter Midtown. However, with the proposed ramp conversion,
drivers would be less likely to make a left at Abel Street because the new ramp would provide a more
direct route for some destinations within Midtown. Overall, for drivers entering Midtown, the ramp
conversion would result in fewer trips eastbound on Serra Way and fewer trips for the eastbound left turn
movement at the Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard intersection. The ramp conversion would result in more
eastbound through trips at the intersection of Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard.

The peak hour diversion generated by Phases 1 and 2 of the proposed ramp conversion were assigned to
the roadway system in accordance with the trip redistribution patterns discussed above. None of the other
project improvements would result in significant traffic diversion. Project trip volumes are tabulated in
Appendix F.


Project Traffic Volumes
The Phase 1 and 2 diversion of traffic due to the planned improvements was added to Near Term No
Project traffic volumes to obtain project traffic volumes. The project traffic volumes for Phase 1 and



Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                   19
Phase 2 are shown graphically on Figures 6 and 7. Traffic volumes for all components of traffic are
tabulated in Appendix C.


Significant Impact Criteria
Significance criteria are used to establish what constitutes an impact. For this analysis there are two sets
of relevant criteria for impacts on intersections and freeways. These are based on: (1) the City of Milpitas
and intersection Level of Service standards and (2) the CMP intersection Level of Service standards.

The project is said to create a significant adverse LOS impact on traffic conditions at an intersection in the
City of Milpitas if for either peak hour:

    1. The level of service at the intersection degrades from an acceptable LOS D or better under Near
       Term No Project conditions to an unacceptable LOS E or F under project conditions, or

    2. The level of service at the intersection is an unacceptable LOS E or F under Near Term No
       Project conditions and the proposed improvement projects causes both the critical-movement
       delay at the intersection to increase by four or more seconds and the demand-to-capacity ratio
       (V/C) to increase by .01 or more.

An exception to this rule applies when the addition of project traffic reduces the amount of average
stopped delay for critical movements (i.e. the change in average stopped delay for critical movements is
negative). In this case, the threshold of significance is an increase in the critical V/C value by .01 or more.

A significant impact by the City of Milpitas standards is said to be satisfactorily mitigated when measures
are implemented that would restore intersection level of service to Near Term No Project conditions or
better.

The definition of a significant impact at a CMP intersection is the same as for the City of Milpitas, except
that the CMP standard for acceptable level of service at a CMP intersection is LOS E or better. A
significant impact by CMP standards is said to be satisfactorily mitigated when measures are
implemented that would restore intersection conditions to Near Term No Project conditions or better.

Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                                             23
The intersection of Milpitas Boulevard and Calaveras Boulevard is projected to degrade to LOS F during
the AM peak hour with or without the proposed improvement projects. This intersection experiences a
large increase in traffic in the future due to already approved development projects and the buildout of the
Midtown Specific Plan. The four proposed improvement projects would have little effect on operations of
this intersection. In the future, the City is planning to widen Calaveras Boulevard to six lanes between
Milpitas Boulevard and Abel Street. Operational improvements are also planned for intersections on
Calaveras Boulevard between I-680 and I-880. The City is currently developing conceptual plans for
these improvements and methods to finance the construction. It is believed that the implementation of
these improvements will return the LOS at the intersection of Milpitas Boulevard/Calaveras Boulevard to
acceptable levels.

The intersection of Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard is projected to degrade from LOS E under no
project conditions to LOS F under Phase 1 and Phase 2 conditions during the PM peak hour. Most of the
delay is added as a result of the on-ramp closure. Phase 1 of the project (on-ramp closure) would add 15.9
seconds of average delay during the PM peak hour (94.1 seconds ­ 78.2 seconds). This is primarily due
to the fact that traffic using the eastbound on-ramp to Calaveras Boulevard must divert to the intersection
of Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard. Phase 2 of the project (on-ramp closure and off-ramp open)
would add an additional 3.5 seconds of average delay during the PM peak hour (97.6 seconds ­ 94.1
seconds). The additional delay occurs because the new off-ramp draws additional eastbound traffic on
Calaveras Boulevard, which is the peak direction during the PM commute hour, through the intersection
of Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard. During the AM commute hours, the effects of both Phases 1 and 2 on
intersection operations at Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard would be minimal.

All of the remaining study intersections would operate at acceptable levels. The level of service
calculation sheets are included in Appendix D.


    Significant Impact: The intersection of Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard would operate at LOS E
    under Near Term No Project conditions during the PM peak hour. Under Phase 1 and 2 project
    conditions it would degrade to LOS F. According to the CMP guidelines, this would constitute a
    significant impact.

    Mitigation: The 2030 Valley Transportation Plan (VTP) includes a range of highway and transit
    improvement projects to ease existing and future traffic congestion along major travel corridors in
    Santa Clara County. The widening of Calaveras Boulevard, between Milpitas Boulevard and Abel
    Street, is the highest priority project under the Street and Local Roads category and at least 80% of
    the necessary project funding may be secured from federal sources as part of the VTP. To mitigate the
    significant impact, as part of the widening of Calaveras widening project, the following would be
    required:

    ·   Add one additional westbound left turn lane on Calaveras Boulevard (for a total of 2 left turn
        lanes), and
    ·   Restripe the northbound approach on Abel Street from a two through lanes and one right turn lane
        to one through lane, one shared right/through lane, and one right turn lane. This may require
        modifications to the crosswalks at the intersection.

    The implementation of this mitigation would return the LOS to E during the PM peak hour.
    However, the implementation of these improvements may have secondary affects that result in
    additional undesirable impacts. The addition of a second right turn lane northbound on Abel Street
    could result in safety issues for pedestrians in the adjacent crosswalk. While removal of the crosswalk
    would eliminate the potential safety issue, crosswalk removal would decrease pedestrian mobility in

Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                    24
    the Midtown area, which is contrary to the goals of the Midtown Specific Plan. In addition, the
    additional westbound left turn lane on Calaveras Boulevard results in alignment issues with the
    Calaveras Blvd PSR and additional right-of-way on Calaveras Boulevard. Furthermore, this
    improvement is not likely feasible without the widening of Calaveras Boulevard bridge between Abel
    Street and Milpitas Boulevard, which may not occur for many years. Considering all these issues, the
    City of Milpitas has decided that the Phase 1 and 2 impacts at Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard
    should be considered significant and unavoidable. Because Abel Street/Calaveras Boulevard is
    designated as a CMP intersection, and the intersection is subject to regional monitoring, the City of
    Milpitas has opted to prepare a deficiency plan to offset the significant and unavoidable impacts at
    this location.


Signal Warrant Analysis

The peak-hour signal warrant was checked for the unsignalized intersections of Main Street/Calaveras
Boulevard Ramp and Main Street/Carlo Street Ramp to determine whether signalization would be
justified on the basis of project peak-hour volumes. The analysis showed that the peak hour volume signal
warrant is not satisfied under Phase 1 or Phase 2 project conditions at any of the intersections (see Table
7). However, this is just one of eleven possible signal warrants checks. The signal warrant analysis sheets
are included in Appendix E.



Bicycle Impacts
The proposed improvement projects would not result in the removal of any bike lanes, materially change
roadway conditions for bike travel, nor change the demand for bike facilities in the Midtown area. For
these reasons, the impacts on bicycle travel would be less than significant.


Transit Impacts
The proposed improvement projects would not change the demand for transit facilities, modify transit
stops, nor modify routes for buses in the Midtown area (buses do not use the Carlo Street On-Ramp to
Calaveras Boulevard). For these reasons, the impacts on transit travel would be less than significant.


Pedestrian Impacts
The proposed improvement projects would not change the demand for pedestrian facilities nor materially
change roadway conditions for pedestrian travel in the Midtown area. For these reasons, the impacts on
pedestrian travel would be less than significant.

5.
Year 2030 Conditions
This chapter presents a summary of the traffic conditions that would occur under year 2030 conditions
with the proposed improvement projects (hereafter referred to as Project 2030). The analysis of 2030
project conditions was conducted based on projected roadway link volumes using year 2030 land use
data. AM and PM peak hour volumes were developed using the Valley Transportation Authority (VTA)
Congestion Management Program (CMP) year 2030 Travel Demand Forecast (TDF) model. All traffic
volumes for year 2030 were supplied by the McCarthy Ranch R&D Traffic Impact Analysis dated
September 25, 2007. To determine project impacts, year 2030 traffic conditions without the proposed
projects (hereafter referred to as No Project 2030) were compared to traffic conditions with proposed
improvement projects (Project 2030). Unlike the near-term analysis described in the previous chapter, the
analysis of 2030 conditions was conducted only for the full build out of the four proposed improvement
projects (Phase 2 only). Phase 1 (onramp closure only) represents an interim condition likely to occur
during construction of the new off-ramp. It would be completed well in advance of 2030.


Project Impact Criteria
For cumulative conditions, the traffic operations at the study segments were evaluated based on the
volume-to-capacity ratio, which can be correlated to a level of service. Under year 2030 conditions, a
project is said to adversely impact a roadway segment if:

    ·   The roadway segment is projected to operate below its LOS standard under No Project 2030 and
        the proposed project is projected to cause an increase in traffic of at least one percent of its
        capacity. Or

    ·   The roadway segment is projected to operate at or better than its LOS standard under No Project
        2030 and the proposed project is expected to degrade the level of service to less than acceptable
        levels.


Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                   27
On roadway segments under year 2030 conditions, a project is said to benefit a roadway segment if:

    ·   The roadway segment is projected to operate below its LOS standard under No Project 2030 and
        the proposed project is expected to cause a decrease in traffic of at least one percent of its
        capacity.

For CMP roadway segments, the minimum acceptable level of service is LOS E. At roadway segments in
Milpitas that are not CMP roadway segments, the minimum acceptable level of service is LOS D.
Calaveras Boulevard, Montague Expressway, I-880, and SR 237 are the only CMP roadways analyzed for
this study.


2030 Network Assumptions
The year 2030 network assumptions under project and no project conditions are described below.

No Project 2030

The year 2030 roadway network for the no project scenario includes planned transportation
improvements. The improvements included in the VTA CMP TDF model have a high probability of
receiving funding in the future. Within the study area, the following improvements were included:

    ·   I-880 Widening Projects. I-880 will be widened to include a high occupancy vehicle lane and
        auxiliary lane in each direction from Montague Expressway north into Alameda County.

    ·   Fremont Boulevard Extension to Dixon Landing Road. Fremont Boulevard will be extended
        southward from its current terminus near Lakeview Drive to Dixon Landing Road. The Fremont
        Boulevard extension will include two lanes in each direction and will form the forth leg of the
        McCarthy Boulevard/Dixon Landing Road intersection. The Fremont Boulevard Extension is a
        City of Fremont (developer funded) project and will occur when the King-Lyon property
        develops.

    ·   Calaveras Boulevard. Calaveras Boulevard will be widened to six lanes between Milpitas
        Boulevard and Abel Street. Operational improvements are also planned for intersections on
        Calaveras Boulevard between I-680 and I-880.

    ·   Montague Expressway. Montague Expressway will be widened to provide eight lanes between
        Great Mall Parkway and I-880. The intersection of Montague Expressway and Great Mall
        Parkway is planned for grade separation.

Planned improvements outside the study area are described in the VTA Valley Transportation Plan 2030,
which is on file with the City of Milpitas. It should be noted that some VTP 2030 projects in the City of
Milpitas have been identified for VTP 2030 funding. However, the City is still responsible for the 20
percent local match. Therefore, additional monetary contributions for these projects are necessary.

Project 2030

The Project 2030 scenario includes all of the improvements described in the No Project 2030 scenario,
but also would result in further modifications to the roadway network (see Chapter 1 for a complete
description of improvements). However, the scale of the improvements would not materially change the


Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                 28
overall capacity of the subject roadways given the methods used in the City's 2030 analysis. The City's
year 2030 methods are primarily focussed on corridor capacity, rather than intersection operations
capacity. The City's method for year 2030 analysis considers the number of through lanes on a roadway,
and reduces the capacity of each through lane to account for conflicting movements at intersections.

For the proposed improvements to the Carlo Street ramp at Calaveras Boulevard, the principle effect
would be the diversion of traffic. Impacts to the capacity of Main Street and Calaveras Boulevard would
be insignificant. At the intersection of Abel Street and Calaveras Boulevard, the removal of the planned
second eastbound left turn lane and the introduction of a southbound right turn overlap phase are
primarily operational improvements for turn movements. Although these will affect intersection capacity
at certain times of the day (depending on what movements are critical), the overall scale of improvements
is not large enough to change the capacity of the Calaveras Boulevard corridor. For the proposed lane
reduction on Main Street between Great Mall Parkway and Abel Street, the proposed reduction would not
reduce the number of approach lanes at the signalized intersections below two and would maintain
adequate length for the approach lanes as needed to not adversely affect intersection operations. Thus,
even though between the intersections the number of through lanes would be reduced from four to two, in
the sections of Main Street that determine the segment's corridor capacity, a minimum of two approach
lanes would be maintained, effectively keeping the capacity of the segment unchanged.


Year 2030 Traffic Volumes
All traffic volumes for the No Project 2030 scenario were supplied by the McCarthy Ranch R&D TIA
dated September 25, 2007. Traffic volumes for the Project 2030 scenario were estimated by adding to the
No Project 2030 volumes, the diversion created by the proposed improvement projects. The methods used
to determine the project traffic diversion are described in Chapter 4.


Year 2030 Traffic Analysis
Project conditions were evaluated relative to No Project 2030 in order to determine potential impacts. The
impacts of the proposed project are summarized on Tables 8 through 11. Each table shows the study
roadway segments, the 2030 peak hour volumes for the No Project and Project, the volume-to-capacity
ratio, the level of service, and whether the proposed project adversely impacts the roadways based on the
aforementioned impact criteria. Table 8 presents the results of the northbound and eastbound roadway
segments analysis for the AM peak hour. Table 9 presents the results of the southbound and westbound
roadway segments analysis for the AM peak hour. Table 10 presents the results of the northbound and
eastbound roadway segments analysis for the PM peak hour. Table 11 presents the results of the
southbound and westbound roadway segments analysis for the PM peak hour.

As expected, many of the roadway segments would operate a LOS E or F by the year 2030. Even though
the 2030 roadway network assumes several major roadway capacity improvements, the anticipated
growth in jobs and housing would cause the traffic to increase substantially and cause increased
congestion on the transportation system.

The proposed improvement projects would have a beneficial significant impact on the following roadway
segments in both the AM and PM Peak Hour:

    ·   Main Street (southbound), between Calaveras Boulevard Ramp and Carlo Street Ramp (AM Peak)
    ·   Main Street (northbound), between Carlo Street Ramp and Curtis Avenue (PM Peak)


Hexagon Transportation Consultants, Inc.
Milpitas Midtown Improvement Plans TIA                                                                 29
    ·   Main Street (southbound), between Calaveras Boulevard Ramp and Carlo Street Ramp (PM Peak)

The proposed improvement projects would have an adverse significant impact the following roadway
segments in both the AM and PM peak hours:

    ·   Abel Street (southbound), between Milpitas Boulevard and Calaveras Boulevard (AM Peak)
    ·   Abel Street (northbound), between Calaveras Boulevard and Great Mall Parkway (PM Peak)
    ·   Main Street (northbound), between Weller Lane and Calaveras Boulevard Ramp (PM Peak)
    ·   Main Street (northbound), between Calaveras Boulevard Ramp and Carlo Street Ramp (PM Peak)

    Significant Impact: Abel Street southbound between Milpitas Boulevard and Calaveras Boulevard
    would operate at LOS F under No Project 2030 conditions during the AM peak hour. The Carlo Street
    ramp conversion would add traffic in the amount of 2% of capacity to this segment. According to the
    Milpitas significance criteria, this would constitute a significant impact. The significant impacts on
    Abel Street between Milpitas Boulevard and Calaveras Boulevard occur immediately around the
    intersection of Calaveras Boulevard at Abel Street. Thus, the improvements to this intersection would
    effectively mitigate the impacts of the Carlo Street ramp diversion. However, as previously described,
    for various reasons, the City has considered these improvements infeasible and considers the impacts
    on this segment to be significant and unavoidable.

    Significant Impact: Abel Street northbound between Calaveras Boulevard and Great Mall Parkway
    would operate at LOS E under No Project 2030 conditions during the PM peak hour. The Carlo Street
    ramp conversion would add traffic in the amount of 13% of capacity to this segment. According to
    the Milpitas significance criteria, this would constitute a significant impact. The significant impacts
    on Abel Street between Great Mall Parkway and Calaveras Boulevard occur immediately around the
    intersection of Calaveras Boulevard at Abel Street. Thus, the improvements to this intersection would
    effectively mitigate the impacts of the Carlo Street ramp diversion. However, as previously described,
    for various reasons, the City has considered these improvements infeasible and considers the impacts
    on this segment to be significant and unavoidable.

    Significant Impact: Main Street northbound between Weller Lane and Calaveras Boulevard Ramp
    would operate at LOS F under No Project 2030 conditions during the PM peak hour. The Carlo Street
    ramp conversion would add traffic in the amount of 2.8% of capacity to this segment. According to
    the Milpitas significance criteria, this would constitute a significant impact. Mitigation of significant
    project impacts on these segments of Main Street would require roadway widening to construct
    additional through lanes, thereby increasing roadway capacity. However, widening is not consistent
    with the City's North Main Street Streetscape Project, which is currently under construction and is
    intended to create a more walkable environment. Therefore, the significant impacts on this segment
    should be considered significant and unavoidable.

    Significant Impact: Main Street northbound between Calaveras Boulevard Ramp and Carlo
    Street Ramp would operate at LOS F under No Project 2030 conditions during the PM peak hour.
    The Carlo Street ramp conversion would add traffic in the amount of 2.1% of capacity to this
    segment. According to the Milpitas significance criteria, this would constitute a significant
    impact. Mitigation of significant project impacts on these segments of Main Street would require
    roadway widening to construct additional through lanes, thereby increasing roadway capacity.
    However, widening is not consistent with the City's North Main Street Streetscape Project, which
    is currently under construction and is intended to create a more walkable environment. Therefore,
    the significant impacts on this segment should be considered significant and unavoidable.
